On Fri, Sep 19, 2025 at 5:45 PM Steve Maloney <steve@solrivercapital.com<mailto:steve@solrivercapital.com>> wrote:
Hi Ayaz,

Thank you for looking into this.

SolRiver relies on AlsoEnergy as its primary DAS platform for routine O&M monitoring. However, Graham has encountered persistent issues with data into AlsoEnergy. We suspect this is because Solential installed their own DAS at the site creating communication issues with the Also Energy data logger. The data within AlsoEnergy has consistently appeared cluttered, fragmented and inconclusive. For example, the inverter heatmap shows that the site is severely underperforming with notably low output, which is not the case in reality as the recorded production on the utility side shows that Graham produces at capacity.

Please see the attached document the team put together for a detailed explanation and screenshots illustrating the issue.

We should be able to provide you with access to our DAS system if needed.

Let us know if you have any questions.

Thank you,
Steve

Hey Meredith and Ayaz,

Thanks for meeting up with us at the conference - we hope you had a successful trip.

As discussed, we would like to kick off work with your special projects team. Our first project for CSS is fixing our SCADA issue at our 10 MW Solar Site in Indiana. Regarding scope of work, below is what I had in mind - I envision this project split into two parts:

Part 1: Remote review of system DAS, site plans, and equipment specs to determine cause of issue and propose recommended solution.

     * Fixed fee of $5,000 (can discuss)
     * Timing: < 2 weeks from proposal execution. (10 business days to review materials and send report)
     * Deliverable: Written report summarizing possible causes of the issue including a synopsis of what CSS believes is causing the data quality issues in AlsoEnergy and CSS's recommended actions for fixing the issue.

Part 2 (if necessary:) Go to site and fix issue

     * TBD T&M cost to send CSS to the site to fix the SCADA issue (removing the Solential DAS, re-configuring the DAS, etc)

Based on this, do you think you could share a draft proposal?

Please let me know if you have any initial questions or if there is anything else I can provide to kick off a draft proposal.

Thank you,
Steve

> logger. The data within AlsoEnergy has consistently appeared cluttered,
> fragmented and inconclusive. For example, the inverter heatmap shows that
> the site is severely underperforming with notably low output, which is not
> the case in reality as the recorded production on the utility side shows
> that Graham produces at capacity.
>
> Please see the attached document the team put together for a detailed
> explanation and screenshots illustrating the issue.
>
> We should be able to provide you with access to our DAS system if needed.
>
> Let us know if you have any questions.
>
> Thank you,
> Steve

On Fri, Sep 19, 2025 at 5:45 PM Steve Maloney <steve@solrivercapital.com<mailto:steve@solrivercapital.com>> wrote:
Hi Ayaz,

Thank you for looking into this.

SolRiver relies on AlsoEnergy as its primary DAS platform for routine O&M monitoring. However, Graham has encountered persistent issues with data into AlsoEnergy. We suspect this is because Solential installed their own DAS at the site creating communication issues with the Also Energy data logger. The data within AlsoEnergy has consistently appeared cluttered, fragmented and inconclusive. For example, the inverter heatmap shows that the site is severely underperforming with notably low output, which is not the case in reality as the recorded production on the utility side shows that Graham produces at capacity.

Please see the attached document the team put together for a detailed explanation and screenshots illustrating the issue.

We should be able to provide you with access to our DAS system if needed.

Let us know if you have any questions.

Thank you,
Steve

> Hi Ayaz,
>
> Thank you for looking into this.
>
> SolRiver relies on AlsoEnergy as its primary DAS platform for routine O&M
> monitoring. However, Graham has encountered persistent issues with data
> into AlsoEnergy. We suspect this is because Solential installed their own
> DAS at the site creating communication issues with the Also Energy data
> logger. The data within AlsoEnergy has consistently appeared cluttered,
> fragmented and inconclusive. For example, the inverter heatmap shows that
> the site is severely underperforming with notably low output, which is not
> the case in reality as the recorded production on the utility side shows
> that Graham produces at capacity.

site on 6-16. Here are his notes from his visit: Checked array and 35-40
rows had been damaged. A total of 47 rows has now been vandalized. String
inverters 3,4,5,6 has been returned to service although a couple strings
are missing. Police report is provided. If more inverters are now offline
again.It might be worth it to hire the local authorities to conduct a sting
operation. I will try and get a technician out there again today.

Thanks,

Jayme Orrock

Vice President of Construction

*NARENCO │ *National Renewable Energy Corporation

### Message 10 — 2026-06-22T17:10:05Z
**From:** om@solrivercapital.com  
**To:** abhinav@solrivercapital.com  **Cc:** jayme.orrock@narenco.com, steve@solrivercapital.com, brandon@solrivercapital.com, joseph.lang@narenco.com, om@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Re: SR/NRCO - Elk Inverters Offline/Not Communicating

Seems like we may need to set up a call to quickly talk through this issue
with Elk. Theft/vandalism continues, and is going to continue to be an
issue. Sounds like we desperately need to get the fence repairs completed,
along with a long-term security solution. I don't think we have ever seen
a site with this level of repetitive theft. I know we have reached out to
some subcontractors for fence repairs that were very expensive, and since
we don't self-perform that type of work, I am not sure we have any other
options to present. I'll talk with our EPC team to see if we have any subs
that can help.
Fence repairs need to be the top priority, but I think you need to decide
on what else to do to further deter theft once the fence is repaired.
Otherwise you are going to end of repairing fence on a recurring basis.

Andrew Giraldo

President & Chief Financial Officer

*NARENCO │ *National Renewable Energy Corporation

704.930.7700 (main office)

### Message 1 — 2026-06-16T00:44:39Z

From: Investigate NC <pi@investigatenc.com>
Date: Mon, Jun 15, 2026 at 5:31 PM
Subject: Re: Requested site information
To: Steve Maloney <steve@solrivercapital.com>

Mr. Maloney,

Thank you for taking the time to speak with me regarding the security
concerns at the Sol River Capital solar facility located at 547 McLaughlin
Road in Raeford.

Attached is Investigate NC's proposal for providing 24/7 dedicated security
guard and patrol services for the property. In addition to our proposed
security program, I conducted a site assessment on June 11, 2026, which
included aerial drone documentation, perimeter inspections, and a review of
Hoke County Sheriff's Office incident reports related to the facility.

The proposal includes:

• A detailed security plan designed specifically for the property's size,
layout, and history of theft-related incidents.
• GPS-verified perimeter patrol procedures.
• Belfry Guard Tour reporting and accountability measures.
• Site assessment findings and security observations.
• Aerial property overview photographs.
• Documentation of perimeter fence damage.
• Observations regarding vegetation and visibility concerns affecting
security operations.
• Summaries of reported criminal incidents occurring at the property.

Based upon my observations and review of the available information, I
believe a dedicated security presence combined with routine perimeter
patrols and documented reporting can significantly reduce opportunities for
future theft, vandalism, and unauthorized access.

I appreciate the opportunity to submit this proposal and would welcome the
chance to discuss any questions, modifications, or additional security
recommendations that may assist Sol River Capital in protecting this asset.

I look forward to speaking with you.

Respectfully,

George

> Mr. Maloney,

> concerns at the Sol River Capital solar facility located at 547 McLaughlin
> Road in Raeford.
>
> Attached is Investigate NC's proposal for providing 24/7 dedicated
> security guard and patrol services for the property. In addition to our
> proposed security program, I conducted a site assessment on June 11, 2026,
> which included aerial drone documentation, perimeter inspections, and a
> review of Hoke County Sheriff's Office incident reports related to the
> facility.
>
> The proposal includes:
>
> • A detailed security plan designed specifically for the property's size,
> layout, and history of theft-related incidents.
> • GPS-verified perimeter patrol procedures.
> • Belfry Guard Tour reporting and accountability measures.
> • Site assessment findings and security observations.
> • Aerial property overview photographs.
> • Documentation of perimeter fence damage.
> • Observations regarding vegetation and visibility concerns affecting
> security operations.
> • Summaries of reported criminal incidents occurring at the property.
>
> Based upon my observations and review of the available information, I
> believe a dedicated security presence combined with routine perimeter
> patrols and documented reporting can significantly reduce opportunities for
> future theft, vandalism, and unauthorized access.
>
> I appreciate the opportunity to submit this proposal and would welcome the
> chance to discuss any questions, modifications, or additional security
> recommendations that may assist Sol River Capital in protecting this asset.

>>>>>>>>> McLaughlin Road in Raeford.
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> Attached is Investigate NC's proposal for providing 24/7 dedicated
>>>>>>>>> security guard and patrol services for the property. In addition to our
>>>>>>>>> proposed security program, I conducted a site assessment on June 11, 2026,
>>>>>>>>> which included aerial drone documentation, perimeter inspections, and a
>>>>>>>>> review of Hoke County Sheriff's Office incident reports related to the
>>>>>>>>> facility.
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> The proposal includes:
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> • A detailed security plan designed specifically for the
>>>>>>>>> property's size, layout, and history of theft-related incidents.
>>>>>>>>> • GPS-verified perimeter patrol procedures.
>>>>>>>>> • Belfry Guard Tour reporting and accountability measures.
>>>>>>>>> • Site assessment findings and security observations.
>>>>>>>>> • Aerial property overview photographs.
>>>>>>>>> • Documentation of perimeter fence damage.
>>>>>>>>> • Observations regarding vegetation and visibility concerns
>>>>>>>>> affecting security operations.
>>>>>>>>> • Summaries of reported criminal incidents occurring at the
>>>>>>>>> property.
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> Based upon my observations and review of the available
>>>>>>>>> information, I believe a dedicated security presence combined with routine
>>>>>>>>> perimeter patrols and documented reporting can significantly reduce
>>>>>>>>> opportunities for future theft, vandalism, and unauthorized access.
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> I appreciate the opportunity to submit this proposal and would
>>>>>>>>> welcome the chance to discuss any questions, modifications, or additional
>>>>>>>>> security recommendations that may assist Sol River Capital in protecting
>>>>>>>>> this asset.
>>>>>>>>>
>>>>>>>>> I look forward to speaking with you.

> INTERNAL
>
> Good Morning,
>
> We've been tracking the operation of the Elk Solar facility following the return to the normal circuit arrangement and the removal of the 2MW limit on the facility. The volt-VAR/volt-Watt functionality does not appear to be enabled and is causing over voltage conditions as a result of the under-absorption of reactive power. The site may still be operating with a constant power factor mode. To remedy these issues, please re-enable the volt-VAR/volt-Watt functions at this site. If there is an issue with enabling these functions, please let me know so that we can develop what the plan for this site should be.
>
> Thank you.

### Message 2 — 2026-06-17T23:21:58Z
**From:** brennaf@caseysolar.com  
**To:** steve@solrivercapital.com  **Cc:** abhinav@solrivercapital.com, om@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Re: SR/Casey Solar - Request to Disconnect Secondary DAS at Graham Solar Project

Steve,

Sorry for the delay in response. Upon comparing the provided drawings to
the photos of what is installed in the field I and one of my DAS installers
who does most of our installs were able to identify many issues with the
current installation.

We think your main issue is that the drawings show fiber connecting all
cabinets together to the main and this is missing. Along with this we did
not see a cell modem for it to be able to communicate beyond the site even
if they were all interconnected.

Many wires are hanging out in the cabinets and not fully terminated as well
which is not helping any of the problems you are experiencing.

No wiring is labeled in any of the cabinets that they did run which makes
us lean towards the removing everything they have installed and replacing
it with a new system. The labor to trace back and make what existing work
and adding/ replacing anything that is not industry standard (like changing
the indoor CAT 5 to outdoor CAT 6) or damaged (example wire does not pass
testing, comms or power) is a very slow, unknown cost and timeline option.

I know you tried to get ahold of AlsoEnergy, did you have any luck at
having them get you something soon? This we think would be your best bet as
starting new will guarantee you are getting exactly what you are
wanting/needing out of it. Feel free to give me a call tomorrow to discuss
more if you would like. I will be in the field and that will be the best
way to reach me.

Photos from my site visit are attached via the Google Drive Shared Link
below.

https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/19OH8NCmREP5YQ6drO6Uo4WV8CTCTS7Qt?usp=sharing

If you do decide to completely replace the system we will be able to
provide a quote as soon as you get drawings from AlsoEnergy.

Thanks!

Brenna Franzman
Project Manager
*Casey Electric, LLC*
2037 Main Street
Tell City IN 47586
Office: 812-547-3862
Cell: 812-661-1570
Email: brennaf@caseysolar.com
www.caseysolar.com

### Message 3 — 2026-06-17T23:58:23Z
**From:** steve@solrivercapital.com  
**To:** brennaf@caseysolar.com  **Cc:** abhinav@solrivercapital.com, om@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Re: SR/Casey Solar - Request to Disconnect Secondary DAS at Graham Solar Project

Brenna,

This is interesting; I really appreciate this. Is there a preffered time I
can call you tomorrow?

*A few initial comments to consider:*
The contractor said fiber was installed and pointed it out to me in the
SolView DAS box when I was on-site a month ago. But I am no expert on the
matter. Are you certain fiber was missing? How can I verify that?

As you know, there are effectively *six* DAS enclosures on site; 2 on each
equipment pad. This might be because there are *two separate POIs* on site.
The system is effectively split into two arrays distributing energy to two
different substations. I am curious what your DAS installer thinks
about that in relation to a DAS configuration.

The site has Solectria XGI 1500 inverters, which can be monitored and
controlled through the Yaskawa Solectria portal. I think this
portal requires a VPN connection for access. Additionally, I was told the
site's VPN and router for this connection is located in the
Solview/Solential DAS box - the boxes we need removed. I'm told the
AlsoEnergy boxes currently do not provide VPN/Router functionality.
AlsoEnergy has since provided me a quote for a router to install in their
box which should theoretically fix this. What are your thoughts on that?

I believe the Solview/Solential DAS boxes contain the following cables and
connections. Based on your site visit, can you confirm these components? Am
I wrong about any of this, or am I missing anything?

   - Router/VPN equipment
   - Weather station connection
   - * A white Modbus cable*
   - Power distribution cables (POE system) that allegedly sends power via
   ethernet to other site security cameras
   - *Two Cat 5 communication cables originating from the NCU and inverter
   network*

Looking forward to working with you on this and I appreciate your help.

Best regards,
Steve

### Message 4 — 2026-06-18T01:29:39Z
**From:** brennaf@caseysolar.com  
**To:** steve@solrivercapital.com  **Cc:** abhinav@solrivercapital.com, om@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Re: SR/Casey Solar - Request to Disconnect Secondary DAS at Graham Solar Project

Steve,

I am available the rest of today and tomorrow before 8am CST. After that I
am not sure when I will be available as we are doing a difficult
transformer set that is going to take most of the day. I can send you a
message if I get freed up though if none of the known times right not work
for you.

On the photos I sent are you able to find and maybe highlight what they
told you was the fiber? There are a LOT of different fiber types but none
of the equipment I am seeing even has the fiber patch panel that it plugs
into to go back to CAT5/6.

As far as the site's VPNs and routers go it is typically in the AlsoEnergy
Boxes not anything that is secondary DAS, so adding this is a good idea. It
does look like your inverters all have the antennas installed which helps
set that up if it is not already. In image-6113 on the link I sent you
these are the fiber termination points I have circled and should be your
patch panel. This is in an AlsoEnergy box and likely needs fiber going in
and out of it to the POI or other Also cabinets..

I will try and get you exact answers on what is exactly in secondary DAS
box but there are several white CAT cables and it did appear that sensors
ran to the secondary DAS in the field, but if those are some of them that
are not terminated I have no idea without sending someone out with the CAT
tester and labels to try to find both ends. I got in 2 cabinets on site at
each pad area. one was for sure the Also mounted on the back of the gear
and the other was unmarked on the outside but appeared to be the secondary
DAS.

If you are able I know you are having issues with seeing everything it
might be helpful if you can send a list of what you can and can not see as
well? Some things appear to have no lights on like the Suntrack equipment
and I have not seen one of those specifically to know if that is normal or
not but reading the labels next to the LEDs that look like they should be
on so would mean there likely isn't power to it.

Thanks!

Brenna Franzman

Brenna,

Thank you for taking the time to speak with me today. Could you provide a
few more details regarding the Solectria thermal events you experienced at
one of your sites? We believe there may be some similarities to issues we
are seeing.

During our conversation, I noted that your team discovered an issue related
to the neutral conductors that ultimately led to inverter failures. My
understanding is that this may have been associated with the type of
modules installed (First Solar). Is that accurate? Was there any connection
to bifacial module operation or backfeed effects?
You also mentioned a "Padcom float controller." Could you explain what that
device is and how it resolved the issue?

On our site, the PQM has identified current flowing on the neutral
conductor (see attached). Given your experience, do you have any thoughts
on potential causes of neutral current in this application?

A few additional questions:

   - What was the DC/AC ratio at the site where you experienced these
   issues?
   - Were the affected inverters Solectria XGI 1500 units?
   - Were there any other root causes or contributing factors that your
   team identified?

the site:

thoughts.

Hey Jack,

Thanks for jumping on this. I am not sure if we need recloser monitoring, but we'll review it. I have a few additional updates below to share with you and to pass along.

Does the current Also Energy gear have a VPN and router? If not, can we order this from you or is this not needed for this site?

For context, we have Solectria xgi1500 inverters installed here and these Inverters can be monitored and controlled through the Yaskawa Solectria portal. I think this portal requires a VPN connection for access. Additionally, I was told the site's VPN and router for this connection is located in the Solview/Solential DAS box - the boxes we need removed. I'm told the AlsoEnergy boxes do not have a VPN router.

Additionally, if it's not clear in the plans, I believe the Solview/Solential DAS boxes contain the following cables and connections. See attached zip file of pictures for added support.

  * Router
  * Weather station connection
  * A white Modbus cable
  * power distribution cables (POE system) that allegedly sends power via ethernet to other site security cameras
  * Two Cat 5 cables that come the from NCU and inverter.

I hope this helps with your analysis. I am very curious what AlsoEnergy thinks about this and what your recommendations are.

Thanks again,
Steve

Jack,

Thank you for the call today. I've attached the "As-Built DAS design for both systems." I think this plan set in particular will be helpful in conjunction with the full As-Built site plan. I also attached the AlsoE DAS plans and old solential drawings of their DAS, but I am not sure these will be very useful.

To recap the situation: we need to remove the Solview/Solential secondary DAS from the site, as we believe it is causing several operational issues. To do that, we need AlsoEnergy's support to evaluate the existing DAS architecture and reconfigure or help repair or replace it with a single, reliable AlsoEnergy-based solution. Resolving this promptly is a priority for us.. Do you see any reason why an AlsoEnergy DAS could not function independently at this site?

Regarding your question about the utility requirement, I attached the relevant pages from the IA and a description of the POI. For context, the PPA states:
"the System Meter(s) will be the Customer-owned data acquisition systems with revenue grade meter installed on the Customer side of the transformer(s) the Utility is required to install pursuant to the Interconnection Agreement. There are three (3) separate System Meters that will be aggregated into one (1) for billing purposes."
Pad 1 connects through its own recloser to the Pittsboro West substation. Pads 2 and 3 connect through a shared recloser and padmount switchgear to the Tilden substation. So contractually there is one POI, but operationally there are two independent grid connections with separate reclosers.

Could you please route this message to the appropriate AlsoEnergy techs who will be working on this? When can we expect to hear back from an AlsoEnergy PM?

Please let me know if there is any additional material I can provide or if you have any questions.

Thanks again for your support,
Steve

On Fri, Jun 5, 2026, 6:04 AM Joe Parsons <jparsons@hendrickspower.com<mailto:jparsons@hendrickspower.com>> wrote:

Brandon-

Here is an exploded view of what the RMS voltage is doing when the flicker is triggered on our analyzer. CH4 is floating so you don’t need to pay attention to it, I only included it to get the timescale. Note that the interval is set to 1 second. This graph takes the MAX, MIN, and AVG rms voltage and current at each interval. As discussed, the average voltage is within the nominal range and would not trigger any events or protection on our end. Look at the portions of the graph and take note of the difference between the MAX (red) and the MIN (dark green) and compare it to the time interval at the bottom. What this tells me is that for a duration of minutes at a time you have rapid fluctuations in voltage which trigger the flicker events. If you can pull the files, you see these events periodically throughout the recording period. Just keep us in the loop and we are more than happy to help to get this resolved.

Joe

[cid:ii_19ed254f9065b16b21]

From: Charlie Joyce <cjoyce@hendrickspower.com<mailto:cjoyce@hendrickspower.com>>
Sent: Thursday, June 4, 2026 4:33 PM
To: Brandon Conard <brandon@solrivercapital.com<mailto:brandon@solrivercapital.com>>
Cc: Joe Parsons <jparsons@hendrickspower.com<mailto:jparsons@hendrickspower.com>>; Greg Ternet <gregternet@hendrickspower.com<mailto:gregternet@hendrickspower.com>>
Subject: Re: Hendricks/SolRiver - C&B Graham PPA

Brandon,

Per our discussion today, please see the attached power quality screenshots and files. I have included two snips per transformer, a Total Power graph, and an IFL Flicker graph. Each is from the morning of 6/1, and each is representative of the greater issue we have been experiencing. The software (ProVision) required to open and analyze the files can be found on the manufacturer's website, here<https://powermonitors.com/product-category/software/>.

The IFL flicker graph is less telling in terms of root cause, but I think it provides a good perspective of the magnitude of this situation. For reference, IFL is a metric used to measure instantaneous flicker levels. An IFL reading of 1.0 represents the threshold of human annoyance. As the attached snips will show, during these events we are recording IFL readings nearly 40 times the threshold of annoyance.

Within the Total Power graph, I would draw your attention to the fluctuation shown on kVAR graph in relation to real power being pushed. To us, this appears as though the inverter control is continuously overcorrecting itself in an attempt to correct for a sudden decrease (or increase) in power being generated. This is an indicative of an overdamped system. We believe that this can be mitigated via inverter tuning.

I hope this helps get the ball rolling on further investigation. We are happy to provide more documentation if necessary or jump on a call to discuss further.

Best,

Chuck Joyce

Engineering Supervisor

PO Box 309 Danville, IN 46122

Office: 317-745-5473

Direct: 317-718-7603

https://www.hendrickspower.com/

## Duke Energy Memorandum: IEEE 1547-2018 Compliance - Ride-Through Settings Implementation
**Thread ID:** 19ed0e9ba90214dd · **Messages:** 3

### Message 1 — 2026-06-16T14:45:08Z
**From:** GTP@duke-energy.com  
**To:**   
**Subject:** Duke Energy Memorandum: IEEE 1547-2018 Compliance - Ride-Through Settings Implementation

INTERNAL

All,

You are receiving this email because you are listed as a contact for a particular DER facility in the DER Dashboard.

The Generator Testing & Performance team would like to share an update regarding Duke Energy's initiative to improve voltage and frequency ride-through performance for DER sites during Transmission transients. Duke Energy has started implementing these improved settings on selected utility-owned Point of Interconnect (POI) reclosers, and we plan to expand these settings updates to all POI reclosers soon.

As we move forward and to ensure full compliance with IEEE 1547-2018, all DER customers will need to update voltage and frequency settings at their respective DER sites in alignment with the Duke Energy standard. Please take a moment to review the attached memo, as it outlines the summary of the initiative, associated documents, and required action steps.

Upon receiving this memo, customers can begin the process of updating settings at their respective DER sites. Our team will continue to keep everyone informed and will send out reminders as setting updates are implemented for each DER facility's recloser.

The expected deadline for the implementation of these settings is July 1st 2027.

Please reach out if you have any questions.

Thank you,

Grid Integration - Generator Testing & Performance

[image: FGNW: Investors]

---
### Message 2 — 2026-06-16T15:23:29Z

**To:** om@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Fwd: Duke Energy Memorandum: IEEE 1547-2018 Compliance - Ride-Through Settings Implementation

let's discuss putting this on the task list for long term

To:

INTERNAL

All,

You are receiving this email because you are listed as a contact for a particular DER facility in the DER Dashboard.

The Generator Testing & Performance team would like to share an update regarding Duke Energy's initiative to improve voltage and frequency ride-through performance for DER sites during Transmission transients. Duke Energy has started implementing these improved settings on selected utility-owned Point of Interconnect (POI) reclosers, and we plan to expand these settings updates to all POI reclosers soon.

As we move forward and to ensure full compliance with IEEE 1547-2018, all DER customers will need to update voltage and frequency settings at their respective DER sites in alignment with the Duke Energy standard. Please take a moment to review the attached memo, as it outlines the summary of the initiative, associated documents, and required action steps.

Upon receiving this memo, customers can begin the process of updating settings at their respective DER sites. Our team will continue to keep everyone informed and will send out reminders as setting updates are implemented for each DER facility's recloser.

The expected deadline for the implementation of these settings is July 1st 2027.

Please reach out if you have any questions.

Thank you,

Grid Integration - Generator Testing & Performance

[image: FGNW: Investors]

---

### Message 6 — 2026-06-15T20:57:03Z
**From:** steve@solrivercapital.com

Hey Ken,

Thanks for the quick call. Following up, please see the as built plans, DAS
plans, and photos attached.

*Background:*
The site currently has a poorly designed secondary DAS system that our
contractor built and installed alongside the AlsoEnergy equipment. As a
result, there are effectively *six* DAS enclosures on site; two on each
equipment pad. This might be due to the fact that there are two separate
POIs. Regardless, the DAS configuration has contributed to several ongoing
operational and communication issues and we need it fixed ASAP.

The site is equipped with Solectria XGI 1500 inverters, which can be
monitored and controlled through the Yaskawa Solectria portal. I think this
portal requires a VPN connection for access. Additionally, I was told the
site's VPN and router for this connection is located in the
Solview/Solential DAS box - the boxes we need removed.

Additionally, if it's not clear in the plans, I believe the
Solview/Solential DAS boxes contain the following cables and connections.
See attached zip file of pictures for added support. These components
should be verified during the site visit.

   - Router/VPN equipment
   - Weather station connection
   - * A white Modbus cable*
   - Power distribution cables (POE system) that allegedly sends power via
   ethernet to other site security cameras
   - *Two Cat 5 communication cables originating from the NCU and inverter
   network *

The MODBUS cable and CAT 5 cables do stand out to me as red flags for the
operational and communication issues we've been experiencing, but I'm not
certain.

*To restate our objective:* we would like Sargent to disconnect and remove
all three Solview/Solential DAS boxes and replace or reconfigure the
existing DAS architecture into a single, reliable, and maintainable
AlsoEnergy-based solution.

I hope this information helps with your evaluation. We are very eager to
hear Sargent's initial assessment of the situation, as well as your
anticipated timeline for mobilizing to the site
Thank you,
Steve

Hey Ken,

Thanks for the quick call. Following up, please see the as built plans, DAS plans, and photos attached.

Background:
The site currently has a poorly designed secondary DAS system that our contractor built and installed alongside the AlsoEnergy equipment. As a result, there are effectively six DAS enclosures on site; two on each equipment pad. This might be due to the fact that there are two separate POIs. Regardless, the DAS configuration has contributed to several ongoing operational and communication issues and we need it fixed ASAP.

The site is equipped with Solectria XGI 1500 inverters, which can be monitored and controlled through the Yaskawa Solectria portal. I think this portal requires a VPN connection for access. Additionally, I was told the site's VPN and router for this connection is located in the Solview/Solential DAS box - the boxes we need removed.

Additionally, if it's not clear in the plans, I believe the Solview/Solential DAS boxes contain the following cables and connections. See attached zip file of pictures for added support. These components should be verified during the site visit.
· Router/VPN equipment
· Weather station connection
· A white Modbus cable
· Power distribution cables (POE system) that allegedly sends power via ethernet to other site security cameras
· Two Cat 5 communication cables originating from the NCU and inverter network
The MODBUS cable and CAT 5 cables do stand out to me as red flags for the operational and communication issues we've been experiencing, but I'm not certain.

To restate our objective: we would like Sargent to disconnect and remove all three Solview/Solential DAS boxes and replace or reconfigure the existing DAS architecture into a single, reliable, and maintainable AlsoEnergy-based solution.

use his water. I have his contact info and will follow up with him if need
be.

consider favorably.

   site at about $6.8 million for 2025
   - The assessment notices sent in *May* list FMV for 2025 at about $2.7
   million for each site, and for 2026 at about $2.7 million each

   audit.

   assessment is required by July 15.

acknowledgement of our intent to appeal.

> On Mon, Mar 9, 2026 at 2:08 PM John MacMaster <
> john.macmaster@nelsonmullins.com> wrote:
>
> Riley—
>
>
>
> While my impulse is typically to hesitate recommending any change in
> filing, my recommendation here is to revise the filing to reflect the value
> of the personal property based on its proportion of the assets in each
> project, using the income method.
>
> I’m reminded that we could not find a principled way to defend the
> current methodology for arriving at fmv—namely, an index that presumably
> approximates the resale value of the personal property in question.
> Indeed, it’s not clear to me that the chosen index would constitute a
> “ready market” as contemplated by the DOR administrative regulations, so
> the methodology seems weaker than the ones we advocated for in the Reply.
> In such a situation, reverting to the pre-existing methodology would show a
> lack of confidence in our own advocacy. While one might negotiate to reach
> the compromise conclusion that this methodology should continue to be used,
> in the absence of such an agreement, I recommend that the 2026 filing be
> based on the methodology that we can best defend going forward.
>
>
>
> Jack
>
>

> Crumley is preparing or has prepared his summary of the situation. I would
> imagine that his summary is relatively nuanced. In any case, I’d presume
> that this summary will be presented to the Bulloch County Board of Tax
> Assessors for their decision when it next meets. At best, we’ve given them
> something to think about before just reverting to some notion of adjusted
> cost basis here.

## Re: Annual Reconciliation Notice
**Thread ID:** 19ed7eabd72e4cd9 · **Messages:** 4

### Message 1 — 2026-06-17T23:28:26Z
**From:** steve@solrivercapital.com  
**To:** administrator@oregoncsp.org  **Cc:** info@oregoncsp.org, cchandler@perchenergy.com, brandon@solrivercapital.com, projects@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Re: Annual Reconciliation Notice

Good afternoon Jess,

We would like to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of participants.

Thanks,
Steve

On Thu, Jun 4, 2026 at 12:23 PM Jess Siegel <administrator@oregoncsp.org>
wrote:

> Hi all,
>
> The PA recognizes that additional time would be beneficial for Project
> Managers and Subscription Manager to communicate to subscribers about the
> annual bill credit reconciliation process given the recent changes in the
> oversubscription calculation methodology. * In response, the PA will not
> include oversubscription fees in the tomorrow’s (June 5) participant
> billing file and will instead include these fees in the billing file
> processed on Wednesday, July 8. *
>
> The PA is also extending the deadline to June 19, 2026 on our request to
> answer the following questions:
> 1. If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of
> participants.
> 2. If you intend to pay oversubscription fees, how you plan to do so.
>
> As a reminder, if you plan to reimburse participants, you may can also
> reach out to the PA to request fee totals that will be included on
> participant bills.
>
> Thank you,
>
> Sincerely,
>
> Jess Siegel
> Program Administrator
>
> Oregon Community Solar Program
> administrator@oregoncsp.org
>
>
>
> On Fri, 29 May at 12:07 PM , Oregon Community Solar Program Administrator
> <administrator@oregoncsp.org> wrote:
>
> Hello,
>
> The Oregon Public Utility Commission approved Staff’s recommended Oregon
> Community Solar Program Implementation Manual (PIM) modifications at the
> May 26, 2026 public meeting with an effective date of May 27, 2026. The
> Staff report can be found here:
> https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf.
>
> The approved modifications include a new calculation methodology for the
> annual bill credit reconciliation. Under this update, if the reconciliation
> finds that if the participant’s subscription has generated more kWh than
> the site consumed during the previous twelve months, the Participant will
> need to repay to the Utility the difference between the bill credits
> received for the oversubscribed kWh, and the subscription fees paid on
> those same kWh.
>
> The By Site ID dashboard on the ORCSP platform has been updated to reflect
> the generation and consumption for the entirety of the annual billing
> period (April 1, 2025- March 31, 2026). To identify who is oversubscribed
> in your project, please take the following steps:
>
> - Go to the Participant Consumption page on the ORCSP platform
> - Click on the Site ID tab and download the report
> - Filter for participants who have an “Earliest Billing Start Date” of
> 4/2025 or earlier.
> - Calculate who is oversubscribed by subtracting the “Total Group YTD
> Consumption kWh” by the “Total Group YTD Generation Credit kWh.” Any
> positive number is the amount (in kWh) that the participant site is
> oversubscribed.
>
> PMs and SMs are highly encouraged to notify participants identified as
> oversubscribed as soon as possible. Communications should include:
>
> - A notice that they are oversubscribed
> - A brief explanation of the annual reconciliation process
> - If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of the
> participant
>
> More guidance on the calculation and annual reconciliation process is
> available in the attached and updated Annual Reconciliation Review FAQs and
> in section 6.3.6 of the updated PIM
> <https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf>.
>
> Please respond to this email by June 5, 2026 to let the PA know:
>
> - If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of
> participants.
> - If you intend to pay oversubscription fees, how you plan to do so.
>
>
> If you plan to reimburse participants, you may can also reach out to the
> PA to request fee totals that will be included on participant bills.
>
>
> Please reach out if you have any questions.
>
>
> Sincerely,
>
>

The PA is also extending the deadline to June 19, 2026 on our request to answer the following questions:

 2. If you intend to pay oversubscription fees, how you plan to do so.

 On Fri, 29 May at 12:07 PM , Oregon Community Solar Program Administrator <administrator@oregoncsp.org> wrote: 

 Hello, 

 The Oregon Public Utility Commission approved Staff’s recommended Oregon Community Solar Program Implementation Manual (PIM) modifications at the May 26, 2026 public meeting with an effective date of May 27, 2026. The Staff report can be found

 here:

https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf. 

 The approved modifications include a new calculation methodology for the annual bill credit reconciliation. Under this update, if the reconciliation finds that if the participant’s subscription has generated more kWh than the site consumed during

 the previous twelve months, the Participant will need to repay to the Utility the difference between the bill credits received for the oversubscribed kWh, and the subscription fees paid on those same kWh. 

 The By Site ID dashboard on the ORCSP platform has been updated to reflect the generation and consumption for the entirety of the annual billing period (April 1, 2025- March 31, 2026). To identify who is oversubscribed in your project, please

 take the following steps: 

 Go to the Participant Consumption page on the ORCSP platform

 Click on the Site ID tab and download the report

 Filter for participants who have an “Earliest Billing Start Date” of 4/2025 or earlier.

 Calculate who is oversubscribed by subtracting the “Total Group YTD Consumption kWh” by the “Total Group YTD Generation Credit kWh.” Any positive number is the amount (in kWh) that the participant site is oversubscribed.

PMs and SMs are highly encouraged to notify participants identified as oversubscribed as soon as possible. Communications should include: 

 A notice that they are oversubscribed

 A brief explanation of the annual reconciliation process

 If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of the participant 

 More guidance on the calculation and annual reconciliation process is available in the attached and updated Annual Reconciliation Review FAQs and in section 6.3.6 of the

updated PIM. 

 Please respond to this email by June 5, 2026 to let the PA know: 

 If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of participants.

 If you intend to pay oversubscription fees, how you plan to do so.

 If you plan to reimburse participants, you may can also reach out to the PA to request fee totals that will be included on participant bills.

 Please reach out if you have any questions.

 Sincerely,

 Program Administrator

 Oregon Community Solar Program

 administrator@oregoncsp.org

--

 Steve Maloney

Director of Asset Management – SolRiver LLC

o: 720-923-1983 | www.solriver.com

On Fri, 29 May at 12:07 PM , Oregon Community Solar Program Administrator <administrator@oregoncsp.org<mailto:administrator@oregoncsp.org>> wrote:
Hello,

The Oregon Public Utility Commission approved Staff’s recommended Oregon Community Solar Program Implementation Manual (PIM) modifications at the May 26, 2026 public meeting with an effective date of May 27, 2026. The Staff report can be found here: https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf. <https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf.%C2%A0>

The approved modifications include a new calculation methodology for the annual bill credit reconciliation. Under this update, if the reconciliation finds that if the participant’s subscription has generated more kWh than the site consumed during the previous twelve months, the Participant will need to repay to the Utility the difference between the bill credits received for the oversubscribed kWh, and the subscription fees paid on those same kWh.

The By Site ID dashboard on the ORCSP platform has been updated to reflect the generation and consumption for the entirety of the annual billing period (April 1, 2025- March 31, 2026). To identify who is oversubscribed in your project, please take the following steps:

  * Go to the Participant Consumption page on the ORCSP platform
  * Click on the Site ID tab and download the report
  * Filter for participants who have an “Earliest Billing Start Date” of 4/2025 or earlier.
  * Calculate who is oversubscribed by subtracting the “Total Group YTD Consumption kWh” by the “Total Group YTD Generation Credit kWh.” Any positive number is the amount (in kWh) that the participant site is oversubscribed.
PMs and SMs are highly encouraged to notify participants identified as oversubscribed as soon as possible. Communications should include:

  * A notice that they are oversubscribed
  * A brief explanation of the annual reconciliation process
  * If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of the participant
More guidance on the calculation and annual reconciliation process is available in the attached and updated Annual Reconciliation Review FAQs and in section 6.3.6 of the updated PIM<https://apps.puc.state.or.us/orders/2026ords/26-180.pdf>.

Please respond to this email by June 5, 2026 to let the PA know:

  * If you intend to pay the oversubscription fee on behalf of participants.
  * If you intend to pay oversubscription fees, how you plan to do so.

If you plan to reimburse participants, you may can also reach out to the PA to request fee totals that will be included on participant bills.

Please reach out if you have any questions.

Sincerely,

Program Administrator

Oregon Community Solar Program
administrator@oregoncsp.org<mailto:administrator@oregoncsp.org>

--
Steve Maloney
Director of Asset Management – SolRiver LLC
o: 720-923-1983 | www.solriver.com<http://www.solriver.com/>
15679:1176751

Steve Maloney

## Certification Deadline Approaching - Canyonville 1 and 2
**Thread ID:** 19ed2d28135946fb · **Messages:** 2

### Message 1 — 2026-06-16T23:44:28Z
**From:** administrator@oregoncsp.org  
**To:** skylar@solrivercapital.com  **Cc:** brandon@solrivercapital.com, riley@solrivercapital.com  
**Subject:** Certification Deadline Approaching - Canyonville 1 and 2

Hi SolRiver,  Canyonville Solar 1 and 2's Certification deadline is approaching (6/26/2026). Please review the Expectations for Project Certification document to ensure the projects meet all the Certification requirements. If the projects need more time to meet the Certification requirements, please submit a Certification deadline extension request letter to the PA team. In this letter, please ensure you explain each of these points:  - What progress has the project made? - What Certification requirements does the project still need to meet?  - Why has the project not met those Certification requirements?  - Provide a new deadline that will give the project enough time (plus a cushion) to meet the Certification requirements. If the extended request is a year or longer, please explain why the project needs a year or more to meet the requirements.   Please let me know if you have any questions Thanks,  Merissa Larson Program Administrator Oregon Community Solar Program administrator@oregoncsp.org

Hi SolRiver,

Canyonville Solar 1 and 2's Certification deadline is approaching
(6/26/2026). Please review the Expectations for Project Certification
<https://www.oregoncsp.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Expectations-for-Project-Certification-v251216.pdf>
document to ensure the projects meet all the Certification requirements. If
the projects need more time to meet the Certification requirements, please
submit a Certification deadline extension request letter to the PA team. In
this letter, please ensure you explain each of these points:
- What progress has the project made?
- What Certification requirements does the project still need to meet?
- Why has the project not met those Certification requirements?
- Provide a new deadline that will give the project enough time (plus a
cushion) to meet the Certification requirements. If the extended request is
a year or longer, please explain why the project needs a year or more to
meet the requirements.

Please let me know if you have any questions

Thanks,
Merissa Larson

Oregon Community Solar Program
administrator@oregoncsp.org

>>> On Mon, Jan 26, 2026 at 1:51 PM Matt La Rocca <
>>> larocca@solrivercapital.com> wrote:
>>>
>>>> Hi Vonda—
>>>>
>>>> No problem.
>>>>
>>>>
>>>> We are currently holding the remaining renewable energy credits (RECs)
>>>> that Waynesboro owns in our PJM-GATS account for the project. There are
>>>> basically 2 options for Waynesboro with these RECs, which are as follows:
>>>>
>>>>
>>>> *Retire the credits* — SolRiver can retire the credits on Waynesboro's
>>>> behalf. Retired credits may be claimed for environmental attributes by
>>>> Waynesboro (but cannot be sold for monetary value).
>>>>
>>>> *Transfer the credits* — We can transfer them to a Waynesboro *Trader
>>>> Account* in PJM-GATS, providing full flexibility for future trading
>>>> (which could include selling to someone else for a monetary value) or other
>>>> use. However, Waynesboro would need to set up a trading account with
>>>> PJM-GATS in order to do this. I've attached a PDF with setup instructions
>>>> (please be sure to select "Trader Account" during registration).
>>>>
>>>> PJM-GATS homepage: https://www.pjm-eis.com
>>>>
>>>> Let us know which option Waynesboro intends to do.
>>>>
>>>>
>>>> Thanks,
>>>> Matt
>>>>
>>>>
